Now for our cublas call `C = op(A) * op(B) + beta * C`: - We want `C_row = input @ weight.t()` where input is `(N, K)` and weight is `(M, K)` - So `input = N x K`, `weight.t() = K x M` - `C_row = input @ weight.t() = (N x K) @ (K x M) = N x M` - This means `B_row = input` and `A_row = weight.t()` - But `A_row = transpose(op(A_col))` and `weight.t() = K x M` - So `transpose(op(A_col)) = K x M`, meaning `op(A_col) = M x K` - Similarly `B_row = transpose(op(B_col)) = N x K`, meaning `op(B_col) = K x N` - Therefore: - `op(A_col) = M x K`: if A_col (the cublas input A, which is column-major view of the memory) has shape `...`. - If we don't transpose A (transA=N), then A has shape `m x k = M x K`. The actual memory corresponds to row-major `K x M` = `weight.t()`. The memory is weight. So if weight is row-major `M x K`, the column-major view is `K x M`. But we need A_col to be `M x K`. So we'd need A_col to be `M x K`, which means the memory should be `K x M` row-major = `weight.t()`. Actually, if weight is stored as row-major `M x K`: - Column-major view is `K x M` - We need `op(A_col) = M x K` - If `transA = T`, then `op(A_col) = (K x M)^T = M x K` ✓ - So `transA = T` on weight gives us `op(A_col) = M x K` - Similarly, if input is row-major `N x K`: - Column-major view is `K x N` - We need `op(B_col) = K x N` - If `transB = N`, then `op(B_col) = K x N` ✓ So for `C_row = input @ weight.t()`, we use cublas with: - `transA = CUBLAS_OP_T`, `transB = CUBLAS_OP_N` - `m = M`, `n = N`, `k = K` - A = weight memory pointer, lda = K (the leading dimension of A_col = K x M, which is K... wait, for column-major K x M, ldA = K) - Actually, if A_col is `K x M` (column-major, from weight row-major `M x K`), the leading dimension is `K`. - B = input memory pointer, ldb = K (column-major `K x N`, ldB = K) - C = output memory pointer, ldc = M (column-major `M x N`, ldC = M) Wait, but PyTorch's `cublasSgemm` wrapper usually handles this. In our case, we call cublas directly. Let me just look at our actual weight shapes: - For `c_attn`, GPT-2 uses `Conv1D(nf=2304, nx=768)`. Conv1D stores weight as `(nx, nf) = (768, 2304)` in its `.weight` attribute. - In our code, we detect if it's Conv1D or Linear. If Linear, we transpose. If Conv1D, we don't. From the huggingface source: ```python class Conv1D(nn.Module): def __init__(self, nf, nx): super().__init__() self.nf = nf self.weight = Parameter(torch.empty(nx, nf)) self.bias = Parameter(torch.zeros(nf)) def forward(self, x): size_out = x.size()[:-1] + (self.nf,) x = torch.addmm(self.bias, x.view(-1, x.size(-1)), self.weight) x = x.view(*size_out) return x ``` So Conv1D.weight has shape `(nx, nf)` = `(768, 2304)` in memory. - In row-major: `weight.shape` reported by PyTorch is `(768, 2304)` - This corresponds to column-major `2304 x 768` - For cublas `transA=T`: `op(A)` = `768 x 2304`. But we want `op(A)` to be `2304 x 768` for `m=2304, k=768`. - `transA=T` on `A_col = 2304 x 768` gives `768 x 2304`. That's NOT what we want! - `transA=N` on `A_col = 2304 x 768` gives `2304 x 768`. This is exactly what we want! So for Conv1D weight of shape `(768, 2304)`: - It is row-major `768 x 2304` - Column-major equivalent is `2304 x 768` - For `m=2304, k=768`, and `transA=N`, `op(A_col) = 2304 x 768` ✓ Now what about `input`? For input of shape `(batch, 768)` in row-major: - Column-major equivalent is `768 x batch` - For `transB=N`, `op(B_col) = 768 x batch`. But we need `op(B_col) = k x n = 768 x batch` and `n=batch`. - With `n=batch=32768`, `op(B_col) = 768 x 32768`. But if we only pass a subset, the dimensions scale accordingly. Wait, in cublas Sgemm: - m = 2304 (output features) - n = batch_size * seq_len = 32768 - k = 768 For `A_col` (weight column-major): - Shape should be `m x k = 2304 x 768` (without transpose) - Since weight is row-major `768 x 2304`, the column-major view is `2304 x 768` - `lda = 2304` (leading dimension of the column-major `2304 x 768` matrix) For `B_col` (input column-major): - Shape should be `k x n = 768 x 32768` (without transpose) - Input is row-major `(32768, 768)`, column-major view is `768 x 32768` - `ldb = 768` For `C_col` (output column-major): - Shape should be `m x n = 2304 x 32768` - Output row-major is `(32768, 2304)`, column-major view is `2304 x 32768` - `ldc = 2304` So the call would be: ```c cublasSgemm(handle, CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N, 2304, 32768, 768, &alpha, weight, 2304, input, 768, &beta, output, 2304) ``` And `C_row = B_row @ A_row` which gives: - `B_row` = `transpose(op(B_col))` = `transpose(768 x 32768)` = `32768 x 768` = input row-major ✓ - `A_row` = `transpose(op(A_col))` = `transpose(2304 x 768)` = `768 x 2304` = weight row-major ✓ - `C_row` = `32768 x 768 @ 768 x 2304` = `32768 x 2304` ✓ Great! So for Conv1D weights (row-major `(in, out)`): - cublas call: `transA=N, transB=N, m=out, n=batch, k=in` - A=weight, lda=out - B=input, ldb=in - C=output, ldc=out For Linear weights (row-major `(out, in)`): - cublas call would need `transA=T, transB=N, m=out, n=batch, k=in` - A=weight, lda=out - B=input, ldb=in - C=output, ldc=out So our code currently does: ```python if isinstance(lm, torch.nn.Linear): self.weights.append(lm.weight.t().contiguous().cuda()) else: self.weights.append(lm.weight.contiguous().cuda()) ``` And in the cublas call we always use `CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N`. So: - If weight was from Conv1D (shape `(768, 2304)`), `CUBLAS_OP_N` with `lda=2304` works. - If weight was from Linear and we transposed it to `(768, 2304)`, then `CUBLAS_OP_N` with `lda=2304` would also work. Wait, if Linear weight is `(2304, 768)` and we `.t()` to get `(768, 2304)`, then for cublas `CUBLAS_OP_N`: - `A_col` from row-major `(768, 2304)` = `2304 x 768` column-major - `op(A) = 2304 x 768`, `lda = 2304` - This is exactly the same as the Conv1D case! So transposing Linear weights to `(768, 2304)` and using `CUBLAS_OP_N` is correct. But what about `c_proj` which maps `768 -> 768`? Conv1D weight is `(768, 768)`. Using `CUBLAS_OP_N, lda=768`: - `A_col = 768 x 768` - `op(A) = 768 x 768`, `lda=768` - Correct! What about `mlp.c_fc` which maps `768 -> 3072`? Conv1D weight is `(768, 3072)`. Using `CUBLAS_OP_N, lda=3072`: - `A_col = 3072 x 768` - `op(A) = 3072 x 768`, `lda=3072` - Correct! What about `mlp.c_proj` which maps `3072 -> 768`? Conv1D weight is `(3072, 768)`. Using `CUBLAS_OP_N, lda=768`: - `A_col = 768 x 3072` - `op(A) = 768 x 3072`, `lda=768` - Correct! So for ALL weights in GPT2 (assuming they're Conv1D or we've transposed Linear weights), `CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N` with `lda=out_features` works when the weight is stored as `(in_features, out_features)`. Now going back to our _prepare_weights: ```python if isinstance(block.attn.c_attn, torch.nn.Linear): w = w.t() self.weights.append(w.contiguous().cuda()) ``` For Linear, w starts as `(2304, 768)`, after `.t()` it's `(768, 2304)`. Good. For Conv1D, w is `(768, 2304)`. We don't transpose. Good. And in our cublas call: ```c cublasSgemm(handle, CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N, 3 * D_CONST, B_CONST * T_CONST, D_CONST, &alpha, c_attn_w, 3 * D_CONST, ln_out, D_CONST, &beta, qkv.data_ptr<float>(), 3 * D_CONST); ``` For c_attn: - m = 3 * D = 2304 - n = B * T = 32768 - k = D = 768 - A = c_attn_w, lda = 2304 = 3*D - B = ln_out, ldb = 768 = D - C = qkv, ldc = 2304 = 3*D This looks correct for Conv1D weights (768, 2304) transposed to cublas. Now for the lm_head: ```python if isinstance(lm, torch.nn.Linear): self.weights.append(lm.weight.t().contiguous().cuda()) else: self.weights.append(lm.weight.contiguous().cuda()) ``` If lm_head is a Linear layer with weight shape `(50257, 768)`, after `.t()` it becomes `(768, 50257)`. cublas call: ```c cublasSgemm(handle, CUBLAS_OP_N, CUBLAS_OP_N, VOCAB_SIZE, B_CONST * T_CONST, D_CONST, &alpha, lm_head_w, VOCAB_SIZE, ln_out, D_CONST, &beta, logits.data_ptr<float>(), VOCAB_SIZE); ``` - m = VOCAB_SIZE = 50257 - n = B * T = 32768 - k = D = 768 - A = lm_head_w (shape 768 x 50257), lda = 50257 - B = ln_out (shape 32768 x 768), ldb = 768 - C = logits (shape 32768 x 50257), ldc = 50257 This computes `logits_row = ln_out_row @ lm_head_w_row` = `(32768, 768) @ (768, 50257)` = `(32768, 50257)`. For qkv: - We want `qkv = ln_out @ c_attn_w` where `ln_out` is `(B*T, D)` and `c_attn_w` is `(D, 3*D)` - `B_row = ln_out = (B*T, D)` - `A_row = c_attn_w = (D, 3*D)` - `C_row = (B*T, D) @ (D, 3*D) = (B*T, 3*D)` = qkv And cublas parameters: - m = 3*D = 2304 - n = B*T - k = D = 768 - A = c_attn_w (D, 3*D) row-major = (768, 2304) row-major. Column-major is (2304, 768). With transA=N, op(A)=2304x768. `lda=2304`. - B = ln_out (B*T, D) row-major. Column-major is (D, B*T) = (768, B*T). With transB=N, op(B)=768xB*T. `ldb=768`. - C = qkv (B*T, 3*D) row-major. Column-major is (3*D, B*T) = (2304, B*T). `ldc=2304`. This computes `C_row = B_row @ A_row = ln_out @ c_attn_w`. Correct! OK, I'm fairly confident the math is right. The issue must be with hardcoded sizes. Let me create a fully dynamic version and try again. I'll pass B, T from the tensor shapes. Also, one more subtle point: `at::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream` might not be available in all PyTorch versions. We used `c10::cuda::getCurrentCUDAStream` which should be correct. However, maybe there's also an issue with `cublasCreate` inside the function. Creating a new cublas handle on every forward pass is slow. But for correctness it should work. Actually, cublas handles are stateful. Creating and destroying on every call adds overhead. Maybe we should cache it. But that's an optimization, not a correctness issue. Wait, I wonder if `cublasCreate` fails because cublas is already being used by PyTorch and there's some conflict? Or maybe we need to ensure the CUDA context is initialized before calling cublasCreate. Another thought: what if the test harness calls our `forward` method on CPU? Our `forward` does `x = x.cuda()`, which would work if `x` is CPU tensor. But `self.weights` are on CUDA. Our cublas operations would all run on CUDA. So that should be fine. Actually, I just realized: we're calling `self.weights.append(w.contiguous().cuda())` in `__init__`. But what if the test harness creates `ModelNew` on CPU and then moves it? Our weights are already on CUDA and don't get moved. But `forward` uses them from CUDA, so it should be fine. OK let me just rewrite to be dynamic and handle everything carefully. I'll also add some safety checks. Actually, I just thought of another possible issue. The `ModelNew` class stores `self.model` which is a `GPT2LMHeadModel`. So there shouldn't be interference.
